## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves modeling the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position x, velocity v, and time t. In classical mechanics, the equation of motion for nonlinear oscillators includes restoring forces (functions of x), damping terms (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Cubic nonlinear restoring (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (Duffing oscillator with cubic nonlinearity)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping dependent on position)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (velocity-squared damping preserving sign)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced Duffing oscillator)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (position-dependent stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type dissipation)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Mixed nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * v (nonlinear coupling between x and v)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (quadratic nonlinear restoring force)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) â†’ symmetric potential wells, preserving oscillator symmetry
- Even-power restoring terms (x**2) â†’ asymmetric potential, indicating broken symmetry in the oscillator
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v â†’ linear energy dissipation or injection (damping/anti-damping)
- Terms like (1 - c*x**2)*v â†’ amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles)
- Trigonometric functions of t (sin/cos) â†’ external periodic driving forces or parametric excitation
- Products x*v â†’ nonlinear coupling indicating position-dependent damping or energy transfer between modes
- Cubic position terms x**3 â†’ Duffing-type hardening (positive coefficient) or softening (negative coefficient) spring behavior
- Velocity cubed v**3 â†’ Rayleigh-type dissipation modeling nonlinear friction or aerodynamic drag
